[?2004l[?1h=[33mcommit c26d8a8b54fcb776f876f5ead2e69739271d4a66[m[m
Author: Edward Thomson <ethomson@edwardthomson.com>[m
Date:   Wed Jan 1 15:47:43 2025 +0000[m
[m
    sha256: further API simplifications for OID parsing[m
    [m
    Introduce `git_oid_from_string`, `git_oid_from_prefix`, and[m
    `git_oid_from_raw`, all of which take a `git_oid_t` that indicates what[m
    type of OID should be parsed (SHA1 or SHA256).[m
    [m
    This allows users to continue to use `git_oid_fromstr` without any code[m
    changes, while remaining in a SHA1 world.[m
    [m
    Note that these are not perfect analogs to the `fromstr` APIs.[m
    [m
    * `git_oid_from_string` now takes a NUL terminated string, instead of[m
      allowing for non-NUL terminated strings. Adding a NUL check feels like[m
      an important safety consideration for C strings.[m
    * `git_oid_from_prefix` should be used for an OID substring and length.[m
    [m
    Previous usages of `git_oid_fromstr` with non-NUL terminated strings[m
    should move to `git_oid_from_prefix` with the hexsize for the given OID[m
    type.[m
[m

Author: Edward Thomson <ethomson@edwardthomson.com>[m
Date:   Mon Dec 23 11:53:23 2024 +0000[m
[m
    sha256: simplify API changes for sha256 support[m
    [m
    There are several places where users may want to specify the type of[m
    object IDs (sha1 or sha256) that should be used, for example, when[m
    dealing with repositories, indexes, etc.[m
    [m
    However, given that sha256 support remains disappointingly uncommon in[m
    the wild, we should avoid hard API breaks when possible. Instead, update[m
    these APIs to have an "extended" format (eg, `git_odb_open_ext`) that[m
    provides an options structure with oid type information.[m
    [m
    This allows callers who do care about sha256 to use it, and callers who[m
    do not to avoid gratuitous API breakage.[m
[m

    there.[m

}
